# 上清太玄集

**The Supreme Clarity Great Mystery Collection**

**Title:** *The Supreme Clarity Great Mystery Collection*
**Ten fascicles.** Authored by Jin Hou Shanyuan.
**Source text:** *Daoist Canon of the Zhengtong Era*, Great Mystery Section.

---

### *The Supreme Clarity Great Mystery Collection, Fascicle One*
**By Hou Shanyuan of Gushe**

#### **Chapter One: On the Primordial Transformation of Supreme Clarity**
The Primordial Transformation of Supreme Clarity unfolds in harmonious splendor, revealing the celestial chart.
That which precedes all things is the Dao.
That which ends only to begin anew is nature.
When loyalty does not adhere to sectarianism, the countenance of one who embodies virtue becomes serene and profound—his temples and beard like jade set amidst luminous clarity, radiant with subtle grace.
Delighting in the melody of harmonious winds, he intones the dawn of primordial essence. Unfettered in flight, he roams the paths of the Dao.
The Primordial Ancestor is vast yet without exterior, minute yet without interior; above, round like heaven; below, square like earth. In form and name, it inwardly unfolds the intermingling qi.
Bound by the east’s emergence and the west’s descent, the sun and moon rise and set.
The radiance of great transformation illumines all—mind and matter congeal in brilliance, none fail to respond to its command.

#### **Chapter Two: The Path of Flourishing Virtue**
The path of flourishing virtue lies in its constant application.
Behold the great image: the great image is formless. To give it form is to dazzle the eye, yet naturally its light overflows without limit.
Thus, even one as keen-sighted as Li Lou cannot attest to true wisdom.
Listen to the great sound: the great sound is soundless. To give it sound is to confuse the ear, yet naturally it harmonizes without direction.
Thus, even one as keen-eared as Shi Kuang cannot attest to true hearing.
Utmost hearing, utmost wisdom, utmost adaptability, utmost penetration—all are bestowed within the Dao of the primordial and the level.

#### **Chapter Three: Manifesting Things and Exhausting Principles**
To manifest things and exhaust principles is to embody stillness and receptivity.
Chew and shift the mysterious vision; let jade-like radiance and crimson essence flow forth.
In clarity, it conceals itself in the intervals; in life, it subdues decline.
The mechanism of fortune releases sorrow, attaining constancy; the pattern of pure extension severs the gate of calamity.

#### **Chapter Four: Harmonizing with the Dao and Ascending to Perfection**
To harmonize with the Dao and ascend to perfection is to achieve meritorious virtue.
Movement within the Three Realms is unobstructed only when no barriers exist.
First: things follow transformation—this is the essence of the Dao. Responding and manifesting form is the function of spirit. To employ the useless is the ultimate use.
Second: the mechanism confronts the myriad forms, lifting the veils of ignorance. Shining yet not dazzling—this is the colorless. The color of the colorless is the ultimate color.
Third: the tally of emptiness is not possession; clinging to possession is not emptiness. The emptiness of non-emptiness is called true emptiness.
Comprehending these in unity transcends all bounds.

#### **Chapter Five: Fortifying Nature and Non-Birth**
To fortify nature and embrace non-birth is to delight in transformation. Responding with virtue ensures a life without obstruction.
External meditation is expansive and relaxed; in vast emptiness and stillness, the human Dao merges with the celestial Dao.
Breath harmonizes and fuses; the intermingling qi responds to signs. In luminous purity, the primordial qi and the vital qi connect.
Gaze fixed in auspicious concentration, the numinous bird descends as an omen; the two luminaries exchange radiance—pupil and sun-moon unite their brightness.
Thus, the Six Caverns of Flying Mystery and the wondrous transformations of the Three Palaces divide into the nine qi, converging into the One True.
The transformations of the One True lie in the action of non-action.

#### **Chapter Six: On Gain and Loss**
Gain and loss differ in their application.
To gain is to treasure essence, cherish qi, preserve life, and nurture spirit—embracing the Dao and holding fast to virtue.
To lose is to indulge in greed and desire, mind in chaos and heart in desolation—forgetting one’s root and concealing one’s truth.
To penetrate the mystery and dispel falsehood, to invigorate numinous power and awaken wisdom, is to achieve the merit of resolute advancement.

#### **Chapter Seven: Gathering Intent and Refining Thought**
To gather intent and refine thought is to attain joyful tranquility.
Within, the jade casket appears, resembling the visage of an infant.
The constancy of governing principle and the harmony of natural ease ensure no transgressions; the upright nature keenly senses the mechanism.
To silence it is not to shatter the eye but to heighten desire.
To model it is not to grind the inkstone but to strengthen vigilance.
The transformations of the inner pattern—unbounded and without fixed direction—lie in the action of non-transforming transformation.

#### **Chapter Eight: The Dao’s Vast Embrace**
The Dao’s vast embrace extends without limit.
Above, it covers without bound, upholding the celestial net. Heaven’s roundness establishes its image; sun, moon, and stars descend. Their light hangs day and night, numinous and penetrating—none fail to align with its brightness.
Below, it governs without bound, grasping earth’s yielding nature. Earth’s squareness establishes its image; mountains and valleys fill and empty. Following the seasons, they release transformation—all things arise and are completed within it.
Utmost vastness, utmost greatness—greatness encompasses all. Utmost subtlety, utmost minuteness—minuteness enters all. To extend it is to blend principles; to unify mechanisms is to harmonize all without exception.

#### **Chapter Nine: The Dao Beyond Dao**
The Dao beyond Dao exists yet is forgotten. Following principle’s constancy, forgetting things yet preserving truth—this is how one attains its measure.
Responding to things while forgetting the mind, abandoning principle’s constancy, preserving desire yet losing one’s root—this is how one invites inquiry.
The wise discern this distinction. Such is the seeing beyond sight—this is true seeing. The response beyond response—this is true response.
To respond without imposing transformation is to pervade the boundless Dao.

#### **Chapter Ten: The Path of Inner Stillness**
The path of inner stillness knows the way to keen responsiveness.
Stillness governs movement; uprightness governs deviation.
The law of compliance and change fortifies the substance, unifying the casket. The movement of preserving the level initiates the constancy of abundance.

#### **Chapter Eleven: The All-Transforming**
To be all-transforming is to attain great penetration.
Receiving streams without overflowing—this is the Dao’s abyss.
Congealing emptiness without filling—this is the Dao’s profundity.
Blending qi without excess—this is the Dao’s vastness.
Present in court yet unseen—this is the Dao’s constancy.
Lingering in obscurity yet undimmed—this is the Dao’s principle.

#### **Chapter Eleven (continued)**
Responding to things without cessation—this is the Dao’s transformation.
Communing with spirits without loss—this is the Dao’s fidelity.
Bestowing life without discrimination—this is the Dao’s virtue.
Those who turn their backs on it possess it in full; who can attest to its truth?
Thus do they cast themselves into ruin.

#### **Chapter Twelve: Abandoning the False and Preserving the True**
Abandoning the false and preserving the true, forgetting schemes and severing cares,
all secrecy and pretense dissolve—sincerity of heart and steadfast resolve.
Abiding in stillness, the clamor of disturbance brings no vexation;
serene and holding to simplicity, the spirit’s breath rests in unbroken ease—
this is how clarity is distilled.
Abiding in loyalty, the gourd of prohibitions knows no selfishness;
joyful and nurturing vastness, pure and flourishing—
this is how fidelity is established.
Abiding in virtue, humility veils its light, essence and refinement embrace all;
the unadulterated wind conceals its resonance—
this is how the Dao is joined.
The true Dao walks alone; the defiled Dao is wholly consumed.
To know this as an obstacle is to miss the mark.

#### **Chapter Thirteen: Utmost Sincerity, Utmost Rectitude**
Utmost sincerity, utmost rectitude—delusion and awakening are two mechanisms.
The deluded cling to illusion;
the awakened refine their truth.
Truth is not seen by the eye—gazing upon it dazzles the senses.
Illusion is not grasped by the mind—discerning it verifies wisdom.
The spirit fills the empty valley; abundance must roam freely.
Severing yet penetrating it—this is the repose of sitting in the flowering garden.

#### **Chapter Fourteen: Turning from Awakening to Merge with Dust**
Turning from awakening to merge with dust is to revert to the supreme Dao.
The possession of possessions is foreseen by the possession of no-possession—
gaining it, one loses it, thus becoming a peril to the body.
The use of uses is foreseen by the use of no-use—
preserving it, one forgets it, thus becoming a fetter to the heart.
The color of colors is foreseen by the color of no-color—
illuminating it, one obscures it, thus becoming a dazzlement to the eyes.
The sound of sounds is foreseen by the sound of no-sound—
speaking of it, one silences it, thus becoming a strain to the ears.
The transformation of transformations is foreseen by the transformation of no-transformation—
rescuing it, one betrays it, thus becoming a confusion to the spirit.
Upholding correctness and returning to purity, refining thought and sharpening responsiveness—
this is how one skillfully severs all faults.

#### **Chapter Fifteen: Refining the Subtle and Radiant**
Refining the subtle and radiant—why chase after mere adornments?
Clamor and splendor each cling to their vessels;
secrecy and favor each invite their transgressions.
Yet in the midst of resplendent ornamentation, one suddenly awakens—
the spirit’s eyes open wide, the celestial breath rests in tranquil repose,
sitting in the attainment of spontaneity.
Spontaneity as such is not spontaneity;
not-spontaneity as spontaneity—this is the perfection of spontaneity.

#### **Eulogy**
Seeking the true and revering the teachings, aspirations and vows remain earnest.

**Purification of Heart and Spirit**

Purifying the heart and washing away filth, sweeping defilement and banishing impurity.
The two majestic spirits in serene meditation, severing sharpness and shattering miasmic vapors.
Forgetting form yet retaining essence, shedding falsity to preserve the true.
The body like scattered fragments, its function akin to linked jade.
The Jade Void brims with fullness, the Numinous Treasure overflows with purity.
Supporting the dawn and aiding the subtle, one contracts with the Dao and ascends at daybreak.
The Primordial Unity congeals its origin, the Great One remains undivided.
Preceding heaven through its transformations—this is called "generating the spirit."

---

### **The Dao of Supreme Purity: First Chapter**
The Dao of Supreme Purity, wondrously transforming without bound.
A single qi divides, and heaven and earth are sundered; the Two Modes unite, and sun and moon shine.
The Three Powers respond to their images, the myriad things flourish and grow.
Nurturing the spirit and circulating qi, preserving and refining the primordial essence.
Congealing and transforming it, suddenly an image appears.
Respond to it, and the thousand perfected all govern; penetrate it, and the ten thousand sages all attain.
The thousand perfected and ten thousand sages—none are not within it.
This awakening and illumination—this is called the essential subtlety of the Primordial Subtle.

### **The Radiant Mysterious Yang: Second Chapter**
The Radiant Mysterious Yang, blazing bright across the ten directions.
Scattering the splendor of jade and crystal, releasing the auspicious signs of jade瑞.
Above, it pervades the celestial net; below, it covers the earth’s softness.
Expanding the pivot of the myriad transformations, wielding the handle of the thousand mechanisms.
Things do not receive it and do not live; spirits do not commune with it and do not become numinous.
The numinous nourishes the host of wonders, shining resplendent across the five directions in their time.

### **The Resplendent Void and Brightness: Third Chapter**
The Resplendent Void and Brightness, roaring and blazing with intermingled light.
Its flames kindle the brilliance of sun and moon, its beacons blaze through the bodies of heaven and earth.
Dazzling and radiant, it revolves through the myriad cycles of the numinous.
Freely penetrating and all-pervading, it encompasses the thousand isles in their entirety.
Within, the coalesced pearl is transmitted through the lineage of numinous sages.
Ascending to the Crimson Empyrean’s palace, seated in repose at the Nine Yang’s gate.
The Emperor commands the immortals and perfected to extend their years, their distant lifespans bound to the One without decay.

### **The Body of the Primordial Beginning: Fourth Chapter**
The body of the Primordial Beginning, immaculate and empty, full of purity.
Unadorned and without thing, tranquil and without form.
The formless form that nurtures all forms,
the colorless color that unfurls all colors.
Neither non-being nor being, yet being and non-being respond of themselves.
Neither movement nor stillness, yet movement and stillness follow of themselves.
Heaven does not receive it and does not become clear; earth does not sense it and does not become tranquil.
Things do not commune with it and do not transform; spirits do not receive it and do not become numinous.
The constancy of the Perfect Dao—humans dwell within it yet use it daily without knowing.
As fish in water do not recognize their water, humans in the Dao do not recognize the Dao.
When fish recognize water, they avoid the depths, refuse fragrant bait, and in time grow vast—
leaping beyond Lü Liang, transforming into dragons, thus attaining the water’s mystery.
When humans recognize the Dao, they dwell in seclusion, abandoning ornament and thinning desires,
inwardly preserving primordial qi, outwardly embracing the spirit’s wind.
In time, when their merit is complete, they transcend the Mysterious Pass,
transform into feathered transcendents, and true persons confer their ordination—
thus attaining the Dao’s essentials.

### **Refining Thought Within and Without: Fifth Chapter**
Refining thought within and without, inwardly containing numinous wisdom.
Tempering the true form like jade, transforming the flesh until it is bloodless.
A body like frost and ice—this is the principle of preserving essence to safeguard life.
Outwardly embracing the spirit’s wind, the spirit soars on spread wings,
lightly ascending the mysterious, beyond life and death, unpredictable—
passing through metal and stone, roaming beyond the four quarters—
this is the mechanism of refining the spirit to unite with the Dao.

### **The Mechanism of Movement and Stillness: Sixth Chapter**
The mechanism of movement and stillness, skillfully applied without force.
Illuminating the chaotic image before the Lord of Heaven, comprehending the great cavern beyond the empty valley.
In stillness, vast and boundless, without mind, standing alone and transcendent—the great body severs its obstructions.
In movement, inwardly deploying primordial qi, outwardly blazing the spirit’s light,
merging into the Great Void, pervading and filling the true within.
Returning to the origin, pure and without admixture; realizing the ancestor, offering without measure.
Thus, the wind of plucking the zither—mind without views of severance or constancy.

### **The Divisions of the Great Simplicity: Seventh Chapter**
The divisions of the Great Simplicity, circling thrice complete.
First, the realm of the eternal and peerless, vast and without corner,
covering and bearing all things without fail—this is called the domain of the Imperial Palace.
Second, supporting the pupil and flowing with radiance, dazzling all directions,
nurturing all things without fail—this is called the land of Flourishing Yang.
Third, releasing transformation and ascending to jade-like purity, congealing auspicious splendor,
enveloping the womb within—this is called the homeland of nurturing the self.

### **The Form Born of Turbid Substance: Eighth Chapter**
The form born of turbid substance, a heart washed clean as snow.
A heart pure and desireless, its majesty upright and awe-inspiring.
In movement, it responds to the void; in emptiness, it overflows with qi.
Qi robust, it preserves essence; essence robust, it preserves the spirit.
The spirit not numinous, the Dao not clear; qi not settled, the nature not illuminated.
Illuminating the obscure without fixation—this is communion with the true.
The wings of communion with the true emerge beyond the prior heaven.

### **The Dao Revered Without Rank: Ninth Chapter**
The Dao revered without rank, its counterpart without peer.
Expanding the myriad transformations, grandly grasping the thousand mechanisms—
yet the Great Dao is not sufficient to be its thing, though it is the image of no-image.
Mountains and peaks collapse, winds and thunder rage violently—
yet the Great Dao is not sufficient to be its sound, though it is the tone of no-tone.
Boring through the nine earths, descending to the Yellow Springs—
yet the Great Dao is not sufficient to be its depth, though it is the abyss without bottom.
Gazing to the three heavens, ascending to the vast celestial realm—
yet the Great Dao is not sufficient to be its height, though it is the apex without summit.
Sun, moon, and stars radiate, their intermingled light dazzling, illuminating the ten directions—
yet facing our Great Dao, they are not sufficient to be its brightness.
The Great Void empty of things, penetrating and without mind, desolate and without trace—
yet facing our Great Dao, it is not sufficient to be its emptiness.
Utterly mysterious, utterly wondrous—this is the origin of the ten thousand dharmas.
Utterly obscure, utterly subtle—this is the ancestor of the three vehicles.
Wise yet inexhaustible, spirit-like yet unfathomable—what sage could this be?
It is the principle of the Supreme Mysterious Origin.

### **Utmost Sincerity Without Deceit: Tenth Chapter**

**Utmost Sincerity Without Deceit: Tenth Chapter**

Utmost sincerity is free from deceit, naturally devoid of thought.
The nature traverses open paths—like the dragon’s scales, the radiance of sun and moon.
The spirit soars to the Mysterious Capital—like the phoenix’s plumes, the form of Heaven and Earth.
Its course leaves no trace, its adversaries leave no mark, as transformations unfold within the revolving cosmos.
It ever dwells in the realm of Mount Tai and Hua.

**Transformations of the Spirit-Machine: Eleventh Chapter**

Transformations of the spirit-machine—six perfections share the same principle.
First: nourishing the body without obstruction, the five viscera all unblocked, the seven orifices responding without discord.
Second: knocking at the Dao’s profound depths, plumbing its vast expanse, great elucidation embraces all images without exception.
Third: primordial qi flows and circulates, pervading the empty and boundless, spreading transformation to harmonize all things.
Fourth: the thoroughfare qi preserves fullness, inner bestowal unceasing, merging and blending the primordial of harmonious principle.
Fifth: the fetal radiance is subtle and recondite, its glances swift as shooting stars, its interweaving dense as clouds—none fails to preserve its brilliance.
Sixth: the spirit-lord emerges in transformation, blazing like the sun in lofty flight, pearls, jade, gold, and stone—none fails to emit its light.
Above, it aligns with the Three Palaces—this is called qi within qi, spirit within spirit, Dao within Dao, the three vehicles merged as one, like the Great Void’s image of no-thing.

**Pervasive Illumination of Knowing Clarity: Twelfth Chapter**

Pervasive illumination of knowing clarity—who can attest to its wisdom?

In application yet not attuned to its constancy, in substance yet not exhausting its quiescence.
The deeper the flaw, the more profound the emotion—following the current and losing the source, forsaking the root to chase the branches, those who stray far from the Dao’s standard perish.
The time for nurturing goodness, the resolve of utmost sincerity, released and enlightened, the essence pervades the Great Void—none differ therein.

**Unwavering Integrity and Purity: Thirteenth Chapter**

Unwavering integrity and purity, vigilant and sincere in earnest.
Gentle and pure, reverent and yielding, harmonious and unobstructed.
Integrity means guarding the true with no desire, embracing the Dao without selfishness.
Purity means dwelling in the dust yet unstained, holding jade without flaw.
Vigilance means acting only by principle, following only the Dao.
Sincerity means upright loyalty without crookedness, correct faith without deviation.
Gentleness means yang arising in accord with destiny, qi transforming to return to spirit.
Purity means radiant and unstained, luminous and without intent.
Reverence means ceaseless operation, following transformation without fixed form.
Unobstructed means merging with the Dao as one, pure and without admixture.
Advancing goodness without restraint—this is the essence of attaining the Dao.

**Nurturing Essence and Cultivating Qi: Fourteenth Chapter**

Nurture essence and cultivate qi, preserve and refine spirit and truth.
The body light and graceful, supple and drifting with the wind, riding the swiftness of the Six Voids, roaming beyond the great expanse—transforming without blemish, following opportunity and destiny, responding to change without losing constancy.
Descending, it aligns with earth’s tranquility, giving life to the myriad things, uncrafted yet naturally fulfilling its work.
Ascending, it aligns with heaven’s clarity, weaving the myriad images in silence, unlit yet naturally displaying its brilliance.
Abiding in the center without loss, it merges with the Void’s transformation, governing the myriad spirits, untransmitted yet naturally attaining its measure.
Thus, the vast and sagely embrace all directions, and even those who reach the mysterious yang are but a fraction of this all-embracing vastness.

**The Dao Is Eternally Without Thing: Fifteenth Chapter**

The Dao is eternally without thing, primordial qi interpenetrating the origin, modeling heaven and earth, nurturing and maturing all—all lies within it.
Whether born from womb, egg, moisture, or transformation, all creatures with spirit rely on its virtue.
Waters, valleys, mountains, plains, metals, stones, grasses, and trees—none fail to borrow its truth.
If one awakens to this, preserves essence without loss, nurtures vastness without depletion, refines form and spirit, and merges into oneness, this is called the principle of the mysterious within the mysterious.

**Eulogy**

In the dawn of the great antiquity, the mysterious yang unfolded in transformation.
The primordial spirit-lord opened, the fetal radiance flashed in an instant.
The Yellow Thearch’s luminous thoroughfare, the azure vastness brightly illumined.
Below, it connects to the source-sea; above, it penetrates the cosmic net.
The golden hall gathers splendor, the precious cavern congeals auspiciousness.
Light like jade fragments, lustrous as frost and ice.
Melting and nourishing the cinnabar body, alchemizing the spirit’s realm.
Boundless wondrous principle, unfathomable true constancy.
Embracing the origin and knowing contentment, one dies yet does not perish.

**Treatise on Perfect Illumination**

**First Chapter: Before Chaos Opened**

Before chaos opened, it dwelled in the indistinct, dim and obscure, no form discernible, dark and misty—how could clarity arise?
When the primal chaos was kneaded and split, the initial division appeared: the manifestation of primordial qi was the operation of utmost essence; the movement of ascent and descent was determined by floating and sinking.
Heaven and earth expanded in their covering and bearing, the sun and moon took form in their illumination, the myriad things received life and completion.
Through communication and transformation, it becomes supremely spiritual—nothing it cannot do, nowhere it does not reach.
Called to respond to its substance, employ its truth, establish its image, attain its spirit, and ride its governance and trust—this is how one may perfect sagely achievement.

**Second Chapter: The Dao’s Utmost Nonbeing**

The Dao’s utmost nonbeing becomes its utmost being.
Being is the transformation of spirit; nonbeing is the extremity of stillness.
The path of movement and stillness is the image of celestial patterns and the form of earthly principles.
The changes of the central breath: if preserved, its numen endures to the point of destiny; if violated, its essence scatters to the point of nature.
Called resplendent yet without trace, released yet responsive—this is the full embodiment of yang.
Embodying it fully is merging with its truth; possessing all things is burdening the self.
When the self is not imperiled, it emerges beyond heaven and earth—peerless indeed!

**Third Chapter: The Eon of Constant Principles**

In the eon of constant principles, one relies on feathers to know direction.
Those who labor in transformation externally seal it, internally unfold it.
Governance through stubbornness descends; descent through opposition sinks.
Called round and molded: internally enclosed, externally opened, governance through harmony ascends, ascent through regulation floats.
The communication of ascent, the preservation of descent, the breath of the center—without loftiness and clarity, who could attain this?

**Fourth Chapter: The Governance of Primordial Qi**

The governance of primordial qi divides and transforms to generate form.
Establishing its substance, returning to truth, governing through the Dao—this is the utmost of the image-lord.
Called the origin of communication, the precursor of merging, illuminated in all directions, manifesting the principle of singular truth.
What does this mean?
Governing through nature, reaching destiny, released and transformed, the primordial precedes heaven.
The system of the primordial, the ease of position—this is how one may return to the image.

**Fifth Chapter: The Transformation of Primordial Unity**

The transformation of primordial unity is the division of qi and image.
Governing movement and stillness is the operation of floating and sinking.
Called: heaven and earth establish their positions, mountains and marshes connect their qi, rivers and valleys fill their voids, and the void’s attainment of its spirit.
Is it the essence of the Dao’s transformation, or the blood vessels of virtue’s transformation?
Observing above and below, it resembles the body of a plant, the breath of the central current, the function of a maple.
Called near yet unapproachable—those who approach it grow distant.
Distant yet unneglectable—those who neglect it draw near.
Those who attain transformation grasp the realm of near and far.
Without delving into traces, who can comprehend this?

**Sixth Chapter: Governing the Myriad Images**

Governing the myriad images, merging into the attainment of emptiness.

**Seventh Chapter: The Heavenly Body of Qian’s Origin**

Vast in nature, abundant in preservation—what lies to left and right is discerned through the essence of meaning.
Following principle is the gradual advance of refinement.
Illuminating the Dao is the steadfast sincerity of control.
Called: the hard is the body, the soft is its function.
The purity of hardness and softness is the ultimate of the *Yi*’s images.
Called: the Dao’s transformation, virtue’s generation.
Heaven and earth divide into clarity and turbidity; sun and moon move within their measured paths.
The myriad things submit to creation’s work—when transformation stirs desire, it is ever restrained.
To restrain it is to return to the center of the perfect Dao.

**Eighth Chapter: The Sincere and Solemn Will**

The sincere and solemn will is the heart’s estimation.
Yi Yin in nature—nature’s serenity.
If not so, then refine and polish it, lamenting governance that remains unenlightened.
Called: rigid in form, indolent in nature—this is deep delusion, grave confusion.
Called: silently yet keenly acting, clearly yet penetratingly understanding—what does this mean?
It is that the sage illuminates emptiness and non-being as essence, and manifests spirit and transformation as function.
Soaring and wheeling, dazzling as scattered gems—delivered to perfect principle, radiant at the center of heaven and earth.

**Ninth Chapter: Embracing the One and Returning to Simplicity**

Embracing the One and returning to simplicity, centered in seeing the plain.
Desire before it sprouts is directed toward the primordial image.
Returning to the perfect Dao is reverting to the divine lord.
Called: forgetting its unity, pursuing secret forms and names—when resentment and carelessness arise, it becomes a lifelong affliction.
Exhausting principle is the ease of the constant Dao.
The spirit of the perfect Dao is the utmost penetration of spirit, illuminating the myriad wonders and entering the gate of mystery.

**Tenth Chapter: The Reality of Flourishing Virtue**

The reality of flourishing virtue does not mix with things.
Clear, empty, vast, and boundless, it responds to transformation without end.
Its ceaseless movement is one with heaven and earth.
When emotions and nature are not focused, diverging from the Dao, regret and sorrow arise, leading to calamity.
Polishing and refining them leads to nature.
Called: embracing reality releases falsehood.
Supporting the upright removes the perverse.
Called: like the awe of a formidable foe, emerging transformed with sudden clarity—this is the demeanor of one who watches and waits with reverence.
Illuminating the ultimate unity, preserving profit and purity, relying on Qian’s function—this is riding the achievement of change.

**Eleventh Chapter: The Vastness of Qian’s Origin**

The vastness of Qian’s origin is boundless and without direction.
Its Dao grows ever greater—how can one fathom it?
The signs of contraction and expansion, the swift glance of divine insight.
Moving through perfect spirit is gathering in constant use.
Called: gathering in profound contemplation, governing through the One’s convergence.
Attaining principle—who cannot become self-enlightened?
Called: departing from delusion, entering awakening, embracing virtue, guarding against peril, illuminating the resource of the perfect Dao, shining upon the world—all things follow its transformation.
Called: none fail to rest in their allotted place, none fail to fulfill their destiny.
Following this to practice the Dao brings benefit and enrichment to all directions—is this not the beginning of the profound mystery?

**Twelfth Chapter: The Dao’s Law Relies on Purity**

The Dao’s law relies on purity, profoundly still and unmoving.
Deep as an abyss, empty as a void—dim and boundless.
The cycle of ascent and descent is the operation of floating and sinking.
Called: the virtue of compliance and gentleness, the achievement of excellence and beauty, adapting to time and changing with circumstances.
Transformation’s image returns to reality, revealing the end of its linked brilliance—this is the culmination of the storehouse’s inception.
Called: at the boundary of the Great Mystery, perfect virtue harmonizes all.
Diligent and earnest—this is the tranquil garden of the Upper Clarity’s palace.

**Thirteenth Chapter: The Myriad Transformations Open the Origin**

The myriad transformations open the origin, attaining the One’s reality.
The One reality’s change—nothing vast is not penetrated, nothing minute is not reached.
Gathering in the myriad wonders is illuminating the primordial image.
Called: ascending jade-like radiance, entering profound depths, congealing flame and breath, compassing without corners—this is the rule of the companion’s model.
Companions changing and aligning, black above Qian’s origin, overlooking the myriad images—this is the storehouse’s transformation before the Great Beginning.

**Fourteenth Chapter: The Way of the Storehouse’s Nourishment**

The way of the storehouse’s nourishment is mighty and all-pervading.
Vast and boundless—soaring traces appear and flourish.
Called: exhausting principle—why regret sorrow?
Before it manifests, one cannot preserve harmony, and flaws obstruct clarity.
Thus the sage’s keenness is silent yet settled, open yet ascending—this is supporting insight and unfolding wisdom.
Called: shifting the gaze and entwining the spirit, its virtue is keen.
Vast in teaching’s achievement—this is the assembly that covers and sustains all.

**Fifteenth Chapter: Culmination in the Perfect Dao**

Culmination in the perfect Dao does not cling to deliberate action.
Not relying on nature—how could it be so?

**Min said:** To verify transformation in pure *gui*—the essence’s true perfection—brilliant and congealed in radiance: ah! This is the origin of the ten thousand forms.

**Yi-zi said:** The master’s existence is thus.
**He asked:** Is it so?
**He answered:** What could it be?
**He said:** Before Heaven’s before, the perfect Dao’s beginning—beginning and end unchanging.
The perfect Dao’s origin, the origin’s transformation—this may be taken as my master.
**He said:** Great indeed is the numinous luminosity! Pervading the Brahmā-realm, profound and boundless without limit, it gives birth to Heaven and Earth, wherein the ten thousand transformations abide.
Adapting to every direction, its transformations are inexhaustible; responding to the level, its responses are unbounded.
One who illuminates the multitude of forms—this is the spirit of my attainment of the Dao.

**The Reading states:**
The Supreme Clarity’s true teaching—*Yuanshi* unfolds its expanse.
The Great Mystery pervades all, its wondrous transformations without bound.
The luminous precious mirror penetrates the ten directions.
The Dao-eye is fully equipped, sun and moon exchanging radiance.
The myriad heavens blaze resplendent, the earth entire shines brilliantly.
Majestic and divine, effulgent—refined essence, pure yang.
Preserving harmony, great benefit—all things at peace and well.
The numinous source, the origin’s resource—wisdom severs and unites, resonating through all.
Encompassing Heaven and Earth, merging as one with Qian’s firmness.

*Here ends the first scroll of the* Supreme Clarity’s Great Mystery Collection.
*Here begins the second scroll of the* Supreme Clarity’s Great Mystery Collection.

**Lord Guanshe Shanyuan’s** *Treatise on the Talismans of Yang* **—**
**Chapter One: The Jade Clarity’s Sacred Realm**
The Jade Clarity’s sacred realm—*Yuanshi* unfolds its radiance.
No darkness remains unillumined: it precedes Heaven’s precelestial state.
No transformation fails to arise: it governs the Great Simplicity of the *Yi*.
Pursue it without end, fathom it without measure.
Nameless, formless—
Yet because it is without name or form, nothing exists beyond its naming and shaping.
The sun’s gourd glows with ordered brilliance, circling in stillness alone.
The Dao of Heaven flows ceaselessly, encompassing all;
The mind’s pattern flows ceaselessly, resonating with all.
Coming and going, they meet—substance and essence without fixed form.
Without fixed form: this is called "without form that is not form."

**Chapter Two: Subtlety Manifests Without Extremity**
Sighs at dawn, why mimic the measures of the ancient worthies?
Later schools, straying into side doors, cling to resentment and error.
Greedy for advancement, recklessly hasty—who can remain serene in sorrow for the Great Dao?
Thus, the Dao does not wither or obstruct.
Master Rixuan observes inwardly and attains sudden awakening.
Images without fragrance or luster—first sketching their sorrow—
The Perfect Dao moves from dawn to dusk without cease.
The key lies in curbing desires, stilling the net of cares to nurture one’s destiny.

**Chapter Three: Convulsions Between Life and Death**
Convulsions in life and death—how unlike the hidden repose of the profound!
From life to death, from death to life—
Within the cycle of life and death, who can align with the true principle?
Ni said: The maidservant in the nether bureau, seized by Master Xuan, sought to reclaim her life.
Master Xuan, hearing this, laughed: "Sever your head—how can you argue?
Wound your nature—who will perceive or hear?"
The maidservant, enlightened after long reflection, suddenly rejoiced:
"Now I have awakened to the Dao of governing life and nurturing destiny!"

**Chapter Four: The Marsh Encompasses All Directions**
The marsh encompasses all directions—who grasps its governance?
Gaze into its unfathomable depths, its barriers without end.
Vague and indistinct, yet its essence remains unlost;
Inheriting without attainment, its truth remains unrealized.
Master Rizi, in solemn stillness, unites the primordial and the luminous.
Contemplating the chamber’s essence, awakening to clarity—
This is the Dao of the Three Clarities, self-attuned.

**Chapter Five: The Unfolding of the Divine**
The bronze cauldron unfolds the divine—its questions cannot be exhausted.
Those who grasp abundance and attain prosperity first bestow virtue;
Those who suffer poverty and resent their fate only receive blessings belatedly.
Yet in matters of life and death, gain and loss—
This is one, that is another.
Master Xuan’s words, when applied, are never untrue.

**Chapter Six: Grasping Without Perception**
Eyes that do not perceive, ears that do not comprehend—
Clarity and wisdom have their appointed time, hindered by external things.
Master Yixu sighs: "Voices harmonize with sounds, things connect—
Yet in the emptiness of coming and going, how can dawn be reached?"
Master Taoyi said: "Emptiness that is not empty, things that are not things—
All things arise naturally, and the natural is eternally so.
Nothing fails to attain its proper state."

**Chapter Seven: Observing the Profound and Vigorous**
Profound and vigorous, like water shaping the abyss;
Refined and majestic, governing with orchid-like grace.
Follow the Dao, and the image abides in tranquil clarity;
Abide in it, and the heart finds boundless ease.
Master Yushi, bright as the eye, stirs water with an icy heart—
Not by controlling the abyss.
Profound and unmoving, clear and penetrating—
Exchanging for emptiness and purity, who can fathom its hidden depths?

**Chapter Eight: The Crown of Governance Opens the Constant**
The crown of governance opens the constant, attuned to transformation.
Grasping the profound is like a fleeting glimpse of Yan Hui’s thought—
Awakening and weariness merge with the mysterious, all relying on its truth.
Master Yuanguan: "Perfect clarity attains brightness—brightness in great simplicity.
Vast and luminous in supreme eloquence—eloquence without extremity."
Master Xuanyang said: "Merging and flowing with light, dazzling as one—
Nothing fails to reach its principle."

**Chapter Nine: Responding to Wisdom Without End**
Responding to wisdom without end, cultivation beyond measure—
To measure the boundless, who can extend it?
Your essence and mechanism, eyes that see and ears that hear—
Master Meng said: "Not so.
Your heart’s vexation arises from the eyes’ lack of precision."
Master Shun, in harmony, blooms into perfect perception;
Master Er, in harmony, awakens into perfect clarity.
Master Xuan, hearing this, laughed: "To observe with the mind and exhaust the body is to lose the Dao.
My heart is not for seeing or hearing, nor for clarity or enlightenment.
Not one form, yet not many bodies.
Unfathomable yet inexhaustible, unmade yet accomplished,
Unmoving yet arrived, uncrafted yet refined.
No can, no cannot;
No ability, no inability.
Brilliant and dazzling, yet inexhaustible.
Utterly so, yet not so—
And thus, without being so, it is so."

**Chapter Ten: Probing the Divine Workings**
Probing the traces of divine workings, the image mirrors the true.
Splitting creation, grasping the primordial chaos—
Seizing the summit to control the spirit, thoughts flying like souls.
The cauldron refines essence, keenly pursuing the fleeing hun.
The numinous sleeps in the ancient Dao, traversing the celestial order.
Crystal congeals in cloudy auspices, treasures gleam in misty radiance.
The Solar Palace’s Water Minister, the Lunar Palace’s Flame Lord—
Supreme yang in profound seclusion, embracing simplicity to return to purity.
Radiance seals the earth’s gates, brilliance illumines Heaven’s doors.
The Kunlun Mountains pour forth their essence, rivers and seas flow with their essence.
Climbing the numinous to restore life, the myriad transformations return to the root.
The use of no-use, divine without divinity—
Floating and sinking define their forms, clear and turbid distinguish themselves.
The stubborn vessel converges as one, wisdom and judgment attain harmony.
Waning and waxing complete each other, sending off the old and welcoming the new.
Principles like jade wheels, eyes like ice orbs—
Exchanging emptiness for images, governing with brilliance untouched by dust.
Embracing the vast and divine, enduring through kalpas.

**Treatise on Penetrating the Real**
**Chapter One: The Beginning of the Great Commencement**
At the beginning of the Great Commencement, it arose before Heaven and Earth.
Generative transformations without end, governing the essence of nature.
Mysterious and unfathomable, the root and origin of the myriad transformations.
Luminous and boundless—this is the essence of the Perfect Dao.
Master Zi said: "In solemn stillness, wandering between water and moon—
Not controlling form, yet transforming like the destiny of a kingdom.
Serene and flowing, the clear abyss attains its Dao."

**Chapter Two: Governance Transforms and the Primordial Flows Through**
Governance transforms and the primordial flows through—exchanging to attain the purest essence of Liu Chun.
Its spirit cannot be swayed by the most intimate of companions;
its ghosts cannot deceive it.
Clumsy or skillful, all who awaken to its numinous leech
and embrace its harmonious ease
are employed by the Dao without exception.

One says:
"Zhongzi does not wander—
gazing from the hall, he shifts his chamber,
abandoning the chamber to refine his true seeing.
Is this not the uprightness of the inner chamber’s song?"

**Chapter Three: The Radiant Response of Yang**
The radiant response of Yang—
the heart’s glance cannot grasp its essence.
Thus, the worst of delusions and illusions
gradually attain their penetration.
Who can obscure it?
Know that Master Guo and Zhan the Duke
discussed this with the lofty scholar.
Even at the foundation of the Great Mystery,
though a thousand *li* distant,
they grasped the luminous truth and beheld the divine flight of cinnabar’s crucible.
Feathers and tablets reached the source’s end in the great square—
how could they be bound by the emotions of planted trees?

**Chapter Four: The Soaring and the Joining of Companions**
The soaring and the joining of companions—
its Dao does not act for trust alone.
Leisurely, it flows through;
effortlessly, it enters.
Great indeed!
Its body is vast and without limit.

It is said:
"Zijiao is keen—
his ears can turn, his eyes can perceive.
Is this not the ultimate of the pupil’s glance?
Only the sage,
transcending brightness and darkness to reach divine transformation,
is neither used nor unused."

**Chapter Five: The Treasury of Primordial Unity**
The Treasury of Primordial Unity—
the darksome thread at the center.

**The Divine Transformation and the Square of Feathered Blood**

The divine transformation links with change—
feathers and blood meet at the square.
The sun’s gaze is the emptiness of non-emptiness;
the enchantress is the existence of non-existence.
Here, the numinous dawns,
here, the Dao is born.
Stirred by the interplay of void and solid,
one chews the principle of being and non-being.

It is said:
"The cuttlefish governs the abyss,
yet feeds not on the highest good.
The swan commands its qi,
yet does not order the true origin."
Alas! How radiant are the heart and eyes of the enlightened—
who could obstruct the flourishing of their Dao?

**Chapter Six: The Dao Harmonizes with Pristine Essence**

The Dao transcends pristine essence,
steeping in celestial auspices.
Fumes of jade and blossoms,
orchids flourishing in the wild,
green peaches and golden millet,
joyous herbs and numinous plants—
all partake of its blessings.

It is said:
"Muzi is stern in countenance,
solemn in demeanor—
not the heart of drifting smoke or fleeting shadows.
Forever free from deluded cravings,
restoring the luminous clarity of the earth’s essence—
such is the Dao that may be called sagely."

**Chapter Seven: The Subtle and Pristine**

Subtle and pristine,
startling as a burst of radiance,
the form of the bound and the mutilated—
how could it attain brightness?
The appearance of the listless and the scattered—
how could it govern the real?

It is said:
"Xiazi, alert and soaring above the harmony of all images,
chews it whole and leads the ten thousand spirits to follow of themselves.
From above and below, the scrutiny of floating and sinking—
all converges at the true center."

**Chapter Eight: The Numinous Without Limit**

The numinous without limit—
stillness unmoving.
The Dao unfolds without form,
yet luminously pervades all.

It is said:
"Jingzi dams it—
how could he wield its bait?
Nie’s acuity—
is it not the essence of wakefulness?
Yet these two stand tall without plumbing its depths."

It is said:
"Observe the near, yet do not grow intimate—
intimacy distances.
Gaze afar, yet do not estrange—
estrangement draws close.
Though the dull and the wise may differ,
none escape this truth."

**Chapter Nine: Guiding the Myriad to Seek the Dao**

Guiding the myriad to seek the Dao—
pushing to the utmost of awe and reverence.
The two numinous essences,
like the array of jade tablets in ceremony.
The great scrutiny of the ancient Dao—
feathers ascend the vermilion towers of heaven.

Huazi, resplendent,
shines at the center of heaven and earth.
The auspicious omen of empty whiteness—
not the brightest of daily use,
nor the blindness of the sightless and the dull.

It is said:
"The use of the useless—
its use is formless.
The transformation of the untransformed—
its transformation is imageless.
As for the primordial image—
it has ever been revered."

**Chapter Ten: The Near and the Generation of All Things**

Approaching the generation of all things—
this is the ultimate principle, vast and without intent.

It is said:
"The Dao is pure and unadulterated."
"The essence is pristine, secluded, and refined."
"The qi responds and pervades."
"The numinous floats and sinks, settling the body."
"Man masters ascent and descent."
"The guest harmonizes qi and flows with yang."
"Transformation aligns with the numinous and images the emperor."
"Life guides and unites the true origin."
"Pervasive essence refines the cinnabar body."
"Through the nine yangs, the image congeals."
"Mysterious, ever more mysterious—
mystery upon mystery, from the prepared to the inconceivable."

**Profound and Subtle Discourse**

**Chapter One: The Vast Goodness of Obscured Vision**

Vast goodness, obscured vision—
rescued by plain stillness.
Darkness is that which thins its sound;
brightness is that which dissolves its form.
At the juncture of the constant,
benevolence and righteousness are established.
Who, in calming the heart,
lacks true faith?

Ni said to Yu Yuanzi Jing:
"The luster of Kun’s peak, polished into jade,
merges into the radiance of a precious orb.
Empty whiteness fills the numinous—
the essence of the supreme Dao.
Unmixed with things—
the origin of the supreme Dao."

**Chapter Two: The Constant of Suspended Judgment**

The constant of suspended judgment—
its mechanism distant, its demeanor serene.
Thus it is said:
"That which is neither permissible nor impermissible—
this is the Dao that can be spoken.
That which is neither constant nor inconstant—
this is the constant Dao."
Confounding life and death, mingling things—
the ultimate principle is beyond shame and regret.

Ni said:
"Yu Muzi Zhou, with luminous abundance and refined purity,
embodies the purest virtue—
what display could there be?"

**Chapter Three: The Phoenix’s Harmony and Fullness**

The cauldron’s fullness and harmony—
glorious and vast indeed!
It traverses the boundaries of heaven and earth,
transforms the joy of the ten thousand things.
Things and self are not constant;
self and things are not the other.

Ni said:
"Yu Liuzi, penetrating the cavern of Wei’s integrity—
the crane’s cap, laboring yet awakening to radiant enlightenment—
is the morning proof of the island’s numinous dawn."

**Chapter Four: The Chessboard and the Cliff’s Edge**

Offering only the maid’s toil,
feeding desires in distant enclosures—
heart and things in restless tug—
how could one not be stripped bare,
becoming false?

Like drifting mist,
it can never condense into rain or dew,
only to scatter and disperse—
is this not governance by the already exhausted?

Ni said:
"Yu Li

**The Perfection of the Great Mystery, Volume Two Concludes**
**The Perfection of the Great Mystery, Volume Three**
*Composed by Gu Shehou Shanyuan*
*Inscription on the Illumination of the Great Mystery’s Void*

Vast indeed is the teaching of the Mysterious Origin!
It transforms and guides the lost,
unfolds and exalts the ancestral lineage.
Broad and profound, its eloquence—
no eminent scholar can fathom its intent.
Subtle and wondrous, its discourse—
how could the dull and common plumb its source?
Its principles delve into hidden depths,
the True Void beyond measure.
It embraces the ten thousand images,
governing the thousand truths.
Towering, rarely glimpsed;
dim and distant, nameless.

The supreme principle arises from the Primordial Heaven,
its wondrous signs born of the Great Simplicity.
It unites all forms and kinds into one body,
grasps the palm’s center and gathers all to the same mechanism.
The Way of utmost constancy—
who in daily use could know it?

Moreover, heaven’s moisture nourishes blossoms,
yet sweet and bitter each perceive their own taste.
Mysterious words reach the multitude of scholars,
yet the deluded and enlightened reap differing fruits.
Flourishing yet barren—
things thus lose their essence.
Wise yet impure—
virtue thus declines.
Lose rectitude, and it reverts to cunning;
pursue goodness, and it turns to malevolence.

Inwardly, one attains communion with the Mystery,
heart clear, intent unblemished.
Outwardly, one responds to luminous signs,
the Dao complete, spirit whole.
Radiant—advancing toward the primal image;
silent—ascending to the midst of heaven.
The sky, free of drifting haze,
shines with the brilliance of the four qi’s clarity.
Earth joins Hua and Yi,
transforming into a single hue of pure simplicity.

Yet the Dao’s emptiness,
virtue’s brightness,
qi’s clarity,
wisdom’s numinosity—
forgetting form to ascend to image,
one may wander in the Supreme Jade Capital.

**Eulogy:**
Spirit and qi interact,
their use bending and extending.
Forgetting form to preserve essence,
blunting sharpness to resolve entanglements.
The dragon glides in auspicious splendor,
the tiger roars amid propitious clouds.
Heaven opens in fiery brilliance,
earth splits with dark radiance.
The Dao flourishes, luminous and grand;
virtue stands upright, pure and limpid.
Within, it harbors all wonders;
without, it manifests all benevolence.
The image beyond image,
divine without divinity.
Mysterious and numinous, resplendent—
starlike countenance, serene and bright.

**Inscription on the Illumination of the Primordial Spirit’s Perfection**

Before the Great Simplicity,
the Two Modes had not yet taken shape.
Vast and empty, dim and obscure,
primordial essence stirred,
true qi flowed and circulated.
Heaven and earth took form,
sun and moon shone forth.
The Three Powers aligned,
the myriad beings came to life.

Yet within the embrace of heaven and earth,
humans alone are most numinous—
how regrettable that worthiness and foolishness differ!
The foolish are blinded by partiality,
obscured and lost, beyond salvation their whole lives.
The worthy perceive the great unity,
governing and ordering it, leaving nothing of the Dao unmastered.

Orchids and mushrooms share their fragrance,
yet those who cannot distinguish them are at fault.
Phoenix chicks and unicorn calves share their kind,
yet those who cannot discern them bear regret.

The great person
draws forth the rectitude of heaven and earth,
guides the essence of emptiness and nothingness,
embracing the divine light’s vastness,
virtue transforming without limit.

Yet most beings,
knowing only change and decay,
fail to recognize its root.
Aware of its comings and goings,
they do not perceive its gate.

When spirit descends and responds to the profound,
it guards the earth’s patterns,
transforming with things—
manifesting the earth’s boundless, nurturing thickness.

When spirit ascends and responds to the floating,
it guards heaven’s expanse,
dwelling with the stars and celestial cycles—
illuminating the heaven’s limitless, all-encompassing cover.

Serene and luminous,
its radiance penetrates and discerns, perfect and complete.
Empty and unobstructed, without peer,
it merges with the Great Vacuity, vast and boundless.

Thus, forgetting form to enter essence,
embracing the primordial to return to the unbegun—
one knows the *how* and *why* of its being.

**Eulogy:**
The Dao’s light vast and universal,
virtue’s breadth deep and boundless.
Spirit ascends, qi descends—
heaven floats, earth sinks.
Calming the hun, settling the po,
embracing yang, carrying yin.
The crow flies, the hare runs,
the tiger roars, the dragon chants.
The seal hangs from the moon’s horn,
the sword falls into the wave’s heart.
Planting jade in fire,
dredging gold from water’s depths.
Azure clouds and precious cassia,
white feathers and jade-like gems.
Mysterious light pierces the body,
the round image fills the hairpin.

**Inscription on the Supreme Truth’s Essential Gleanings**

The scripture says:
The five colors blind the eyes,
the five tones deafen the ears.
To know by sight is called divine;
to know by hearing is called sagely.

Li Lou could see,
yet his ears lost their acuity.
Shi Kuang could hear,
yet his eyes lost their clarity.

It is said of profound subtlety:
To rescue from excess, delight in simplicity.
The obscure—
one who rarely hears sound.
Yet the sound of a thousand *li* resounds.
The luminous—
one who dissolves form.
Yet the form of a thousand *li* appears.

The Master of Form said:
Not so! My affair is this:
eyes can see clearly, ears can hear keenly.
Encounter the great image—
behold the colorless color, and nothing is unseen.
Expand the great sound—
listen to the soundless sound, and nothing is unheard.

Master Meng said:
Otherwise! Your heart’s vexation
stems from the eyes’ lack of precision.
When the gaze is steady, it attains utmost acuity.
When the glance is tranquil, it attains utmost clarity.

Deng Xi said:
Extreme deafness and blindness—
if the world’s eyes see, nothing is unseen;
if the world’s ears hear, nothing is unheard;
if the world’s minds contemplate, nothing is unknown.
These three lie in non-action.

Master Xuan heard this and laughed:
Because they rely on something,
observing their efforts to strain mind and body,
they all lose the Dao.

My heart—
not one of seeing and hearing,
yet attaining utmost acuity and clarity;
not one of a single form,
yet attaining myriad bodies.

Thus, without exhaustion, it reaches the limit;
without action, it achieves;
without movement, it arrives;
without craft, it perfects.
No can, no cannot;
no ability, no inability.
Vast and unconfined,
it cannot be fully grasped.
Utterly so, yet not so—
yet so, yet not so.

**Eulogy:**
Wondrous indeed, the Mysterious Dao!
Supreme virtue, utmost benevolence.
The sagely who know by hearing,
the divine who awaken by sight.
Congealing the hun, dissolving falsity,
obscuring the po to retain truth.
Ascending and floating, sinking and descending,
advancing and bending, returning and extending.
Yang’s brightness unfolds,
spiritual radiance embraces purity.
Five talismans converge in the pupils,
three hues gather in the clouds.
Tranquil and expansive, pure and harmonious—
pristine simplicity, limpid clarity.

Within transmits the golden qi,
the Mysterious shines upon the jade dawn.

**Inscription of the Supreme Unity’s Primordial Void and Original Form**

The Supreme Unity of Jade Void,
the Mysterious True governs all.
It engenders earth, it engenders heaven,
bestows primordial qi to craft all forms.
Without beginning, without end,
it extends supreme virtue to universally succor the common folk.
All that live depend on its qi,
all that receive transformation rely on its essence.
Silently it abides,
never for a moment straying.
When it establishes, it settles in stillness,
serene and without intent.
When it opens and responds,
brilliant forms appear.
As true primordial descends,
wondrous transformation knows no bounds.
Embracing vastness and breadth,
gold and jade radiate their luster.
Spiritual mushrooms flourish in the wild,
preserving life and prolonging prosperity—
this is the sinking of earth’s response.

As primordial qi ascends,
soaring through the empyrean’s lofty heights,
boundless and distant, it pervades the celestial metropolis.
Forms embody heaven’s substance,
resting in chambers of jade and gem,
wondrous years evoke distant resonance—
this is the floating of heaven’s union.

The Three Terraces converge as one,
the Five Fortunes arrive together.
Merging into the Middle Primordial,
pure and steadfast in heart,
wisdom congeals beyond form,
easily encountering the pivot of the essential Dao.

Yet Ge Hong’s ten thousand scrolls
fail to fathom its essence.
Hui Shi’s five carts of texts
cannot penetrate its mechanism.
Golden script and jade inscriptions
must rely on master and craftsman to be understood.
Precious jade within jeweled caskets
depends entirely on oral transmission to be grasped.

To lightly disclose it invites calamity upon nine generations,
to carefully transmit it brings blessings to the ten directions.
This Dao is the sacred realm of Jade Purity,
the primordial elder of the Void Sovereign,
the supreme and utmost true,
the mechanism of shedding form and transforming image,
entering the sagely and profound mystery.

You must conceal it, guard it well,
never reveal it to the unworthy,
never reveal it to the unworthy.

**Eulogy:**

The Supreme Clarity’s radiant methods,
linked below to the Central Axis.
Its light nourishes celestial omens,
its brilliance ignites cinnabar auspices.
Essence coils through the chamber,
qi swirls to fill the storehouse.
Golden branches dot the snow,
jade osmanthus congeals the frost.
It embraces the divine splendor of the horizontal;
wondrously transforms the numinous yang.
Jade Empyrean’s net of terraces,
its halos harmonize with starlight.
Ascending to the sacred realm,
facing the Primordial Sovereign.
Blessings extend through vast destinies,
eternal longevity and timely well-being.

**Inscription of the Great Peace’s Void and Brahmanic Perfection**

Within the chaos of primordial chaos,
what stillness or presence could there be?
The primal qi flows and circulates,
pure essence stirs and excites—
then the True One arises.
The True One responds to signs,
spirit and illumination emerge from transformation,
the having within the non-having,
the non-having within the having.
Vast, it encompasses all without boundary,
its expanse cannot be exhausted.
Minute, it conceals its spark without interior,
its subtlety cannot be fathomed.
As misty vapors gradually manifest,
heaven and earth merge in obscurity.
Through clarity and penetration, radiance scatters,
embracing the light of the ten thousand images.
Through turbidity and stagnation, obscurity veils,
the vast dispersal of the One True.
The four births and six destinies,
some depart, some arrive—
when will their cycle cease?
The five aggregates and nine perversions,
following sound, following form—
when will their beginning end?
Yet if one turns back with resolve,
with will steadfast and pure,
a single stroke of the wisdom blade
cleaves the mountain of attachment to seize the jade;
the twin swings of the spirit sword
cut through the bitter sea to seek the pearl.
Mysterious light pervades the formless,
the round enclosure forgets its mechanism.
Preserve essence, secure qi,
unlock the heavens of the Great Beginning.
Embrace the Dao, guard the One,
merge into the land of numinous yang.
Roaming through ten thousand realms,
suddenly perfecting the unity of the single body.
Nourishing the hundred rivers,
encompassing the dual forces’ transformative embrace.
The utmost Dao, empty of heart,
internally harbors all functions.
Spirit and illumination, full of belly,
externally display all benevolence.
The three hearts’ vast wisdom,
the five eyes’ perfect clarity.
Responding without abiding in form,
like the moon and sun’s limpid radiance.
Embodying form within emptiness,
like a blind man entering the world.
Knowing the unknowable as knowledge,
seeing the unseen as sight—
if the Dao can be thus,
cultivation follows the threshold of the mysterious gate,
accomplishing the world’s transformations.

**Eulogy:**
The Great Dao is without direction,
those who resonate with it flourish.
Void and numinous wind,
mysterious darkness and cinnabar center.
Primal simplicity’s essence shines,
treasured radiance of spirit and light.
The five directions, pure and harmonious,
the eight poles, clear and cold.
Azure clouds weave the heavens,
the Purple Empyrean’s Central Sovereign.
Primal qi’s auspicious clouds,
the Void and Brahman’s auspicious omens.
Golden tablets and jade scriptures,
phoenix seal and dragon chapters.
Names inscribed in the immortal register—
their principle is beyond the ordinary.

**Inscription of the Great Vessel’s Embrace of Pure Essence**

The Dao has no direction,
virtue knows fulfillment and decline.
Those who accord with principle
have no virtue that can be named.
Those who distinguish through affairs
have names that can be discerned.
Self and other share the same origin,
right and wrong are of one qi.
Adapting to the "is" within the "is-not,"
discerning the "is-not" within the "is."
What are illusions and dreams?
Like the clashing of blades and objects.
Viewed thus,
who can know its truth?
Those enlightened to principle
dissolve the limbs, dismiss brilliance,
detach from form, abandon wisdom,
wielding the numinous mechanism with wonder.
Riding the primal qi’s prior state,
veiling the Three Luminaries beyond the Emperor of Images.
Roaming the vast and boundless,
entering the inquiry of non-having,
communing with the Great Unity—
water, fire, and sharpened blades,
how could they harm?
Yet if the Three Corpses remain unvanquished,
the six desires do not arise.
Aligning with yang essence then treasures the talisman of the nine qi,
dissolving yin substance then accords with the One True.
The golden furnace’s fire blazes,
phoenix contains the sea moon soaring in the sky;
the jade crucible’s broth boils,
dragon swallows the pearl playing in the waters.
Lead congeals, mercury binds,
cinnabar osmanthus streams with rosy clouds.
Dotting the stars, jade ascends to the Purple Palace,
transforming into jade’s brilliance,
its resonance piercing the Clear Capital.
Jade palaces accumulate emerald,
treasured radiance holds clarity,
resplendent purity—
unlocking the midst of the utmost Dao.

**Eulogy:**
The Dao and virtue are the source,
yin and yang precede all things.
Vague and dim, primordial chaos,
the myriad things blend in harmony.
The Four Ones’ mystery and simplicity,
the Two and Three’s azure and cinnabar.
Yellow radiance scours filth,
purple qi congeals lead.
Qi illumines the three realms,
essence shines through the nine heavens.
The Highest Void Sovereign,
the Central Heaven’s numinous immortals.
Pure and subtle treasured transformations,
Yu’s Remnant’s ascension.
Lush and rosy empyrean terraces,
through endless kalpas, unbroken.

**Inscription of the Primal Chaos’s Blending of the Mysterious and True**

Before the primal emerged,
it concealed the essence of chaos and obscurity;
when the one qi first divided,
it revealed the images of heaven, earth, sun, and moon.
The Three Powers thus manifested,
the Four Directions then became clear.
When dryness prevails, spring generates and summer grows;
when purity reaches its extreme, autumn harvests and winter stores.
The myriad beings containing spirit
all turn their hearts toward the sun;
the thousand perfected, easily guided,
all embrace yin while holding yang.
Illuminate and awaken it,
gaze upon the True Origin’s encounter with the body;
communicate and transform it,
hope for the mysterious image’s shedding of form.
The two spirits radiate simplicity,
the one qi surges with clarity.
Profoundly profound,
emerging from the Qian heavens.
Darkly dark,
revering the Kun’s origin.
Deep contemplation—form forgotten, soul scattered;
immediate concern—Dao complete, spirit whole.
Clear as jade fragments,
luminous as autumn frost.
Still and empty, unadorned,
ancient and solid, pure and tranquil.
The sounds of Zheng and Wei gallop,
yet hearing is not confused by the ears.
The colors of splendor flash,
yet sight is not disturbed in the heart.
Swimming in water, treading fire,
returning unharmed.
Bearing emptiness, touching reality,
exchanging without peril.
A thousand changes, ten thousand transformations,
without end—
what is this?
It is the guarding of pure qi and essence yang.
Before this, the will is clear and resolute,
abiding in non-action,
cutting off sorrow,
eliminating thoughts,
forgetting attachments,
removing self and other.
Embrace spirit, guard the One,
pure and unadulterated,
silently facing the Emperor of Images—
this is the natural Dao of long life.

**Eulogy:**
The Dao’s age flourishes with virtue,
heaven is mysterious, earth is yellow.
Sun and moon surge with clarity,
stars and constellations radiate light.
Misty vapors fly in seal script,
primal essence inclines toward yang.
The myriad beings commune with the mysterious,
the thousand spirits resonate with auspices.
Spirit transforms mercury to white,
essence transmutes lead to frost.
Jade springs tinkle,
golden waters chime.
The three qi stream with rosy clouds,
the five clouds bear cinnabar blossoms.
Emerald subtlety’s immortal perfected,
azure void’s stellar sovereign.

**Inscription on the Primordial Dark-Yang Cavern Spirit**

Before the Dragon Han and Crimson Clarity epochs, in the vast expanse of the Dark Ford’s Great Brahmā, all was boundless and lightless—profoundly obscure, utterly silent, its nature unknown. Then, true essence stirred and aroused, primordial qi flowed and circulated, heaven and earth took form, and the myriad beings came into existence.

Yet among the myriad beings, only humans are noble: cultivate the Way, and they ascend; lose it, and they fall. If one can turn the gaze inward to return to the origin, embody the One to enter wondrous perfection, abide in softness and dwell in emptiness, conceal traces and hide radiance—then their Dao is called victorious, their virtue flourishing.

To discriminate is to invite manifold disgrace; to illuminate is to invite manifold obstruction. To grasp is to invite manifold loss; to preserve is to invite manifold dissolution. Only one who knows advance and retreat, waxing and waning, and never strays from the true center of heaven and earth—how could fortune or misfortune, benefit or harm, ever bring them to ruin?

Such virtue cannot be clarified by settling, nor muddied by stirring—it is wondrous and non-doing. It cannot be adorned to gain glory, nor defiled to suffer shame—it is mysterious and spontaneous.

Vast and obscure! Within it lies essence.
Flickering and indistinct! Within it lies truth.
Formless form,
objectless image.
It encompasses the Great Ultimate,
embraces the six directions.
Dwelling at the edge yet abiding in wonder,
detached from things yet preserving the real.

Its principle is constant, yet seen differently by the vulgar.
Its Dao is universal, yet embodied, it transforms customs.
To be deluded by it is to lose the real and encounter illusion—illusion like waves in a coffer, sinking and floating, drowning and drifting, swept away by the great river’s current. To awaken to it is to shed the husk and nurture essence, spirit-light shining within, emptiness pure and flawless—clouds recede, the sky gleams; mist disperses, the sun shines. The radiance of the Great Clarity is revealed, the supreme real unveiled in leisure.

Primal virtue governs all; the Dao obstructs nothing.
Communing with spirits, the images shift;
the constellations align with their signs.
In serene and wondrous transformation,
one ascends the ladder of mystery to the Jade Dawn Palace.

**Eulogy:**
The wondrous Dao knows no bounds,
merged with the primordial ridge.

Waters surge into the cinnabar pool, billowing through the cloud chambers.
Divine tones ring clear, celestial melodies resonant and bright.
Flowing essence gleams like gold, soaring spirit radiates jade light.
Mystic yellow and auspicious mist, empty white and felicitous signs.
Substance bears yin, majestic gaze embraces yang.
Nine-hued radiance shimmers in the rosy clouds, the One Real blazes in splendor.
A single star knots the dense canopy, the Jade Empyrean soars aloft.

**Inscription on the Subtle Principles of the Supreme Clarity’s Mysterious Transformation**
The Great Dao emerges before the Supreme Ultimate,
the supreme virtue transforms at heaven and earth’s inception.
Vast and formless, sunk in silence without light.
Dim and indistinct, yet suddenly there is being.
This being is no ordinary being—it is called the utmost essence.
The utmost essence has no image; images arise from mysterious clarity.
Forget its form, enter its body—emptiness contains emptiness.
Forget its vastness, augment the primal—qi contains qi.
Forget its mind, shine forth in clarity—spirit contains spirit.
This spirit resembles a suspended pearl.
The pearl has no form or substance, yet responds without fail to all.
In water, it mirrors water;
in fire, it mirrors fire;
in metal and stone, it mirrors metal and stone;
in emptiness and nothingness, it mirrors emptiness and nothingness.
Above, it peers into the azure sky—gazing upward, it grows ever higher.
Below, it plunges into the yellow springs—delving deeper, it grows ever more firm.
It courses through the eight directions, vast and boundless without corners.
In heaven it forms images, on earth it forms shapes.
The Great Void is vast and desolate, yet within it dwells spirit.
The spirit’s mechanism operates transformations, responding without fail to all.
Accord with its form, form transforms into qi;
accord with its qi, qi transforms into spirit;
accord with its spirit, spirit transforms into emptiness;
accord with its emptiness, emptiness transforms into the Dao.
The Dao accords with the round image, the image like a stellar pattern.
The stellar pattern follows accord, accord with the primal origin of the Great Beginning.
Predating heaven’s transformations, this is called the carefree adept,
the achievement of one whose name endures.

**Eulogy:**
The Supreme Clarity’s mysterious realm,
principles still and depths profound.
Primal spirit ascends and descends,
images of the Lord float and sink.
Inaugurating heaven and earth,
its movement shifts through ancient and modern.
The fiery mound’s phoenix calls,
the water valley’s dragon intones.
The Maitreya’s celestial chant,
piercing through the divine tones.
Sunlight gilds the cinnabar cassia,
moonlight illumines the jade grove.
Wondrous omens flourish,
mysterious auspices fill the peaks.
Emerging from the mixed and myriad,
pure and steadfast in heart.
Transcending beyond images,
cutting off wisdom to draw reverence.

**Inscription on the Light of the Myriad Brahmā Heavens of the Great Emptiness**
The Dao that may seem absent,
when invoked, is not absent.
The virtue that may seem present,
when perceived, is not present.
Silent and empty, pure and ever clear.
The valley spirit emerges transformed,
once gone, once come—pushing the sun and moon’s ascent and descent.
The primal qi flows and circulates,
once up, once down—following heaven and earth’s floating and sinking.
Alternating yin and yang,
and beings are born.
Shifting cold and heat,
and the years are completed.
Fourfold openness, fivefold harmony,
ninefold harmony, tenfold unity.
Expounded and clarified,
the real does not depart from the illusory.
Obscured and dimmed,
the illusory does not depart from the real.
Delusion and awakening share the same path,
all return to the essential.
Immortals and mortals tread different roads,
each attains its mystery.
Turning from enlightenment to join the dust,
the wandering soul encounters illusion.
Aiding the upright and dispelling evil,
the chambered soul returns to ascend the stars.
Sound that is no sound,
the great tone does not disturb the true person’s ear.
Color that is color,
brilliance does not stir the ignorant heart.
Losing the constant principle,
seeing yet not seeing—one first falls into stubborn emptiness.
Grasping the Dao’s mechanism,
knowing yet not knowing—one ultimately returns to true form.
Great perfection seems flawed,
its abundant wisdom’s source does not display.
Great whiteness seems tarnished,
it conceals its light and does not shine.
Embrace its origin, conceal its emptiness,
oversee its essence, unfold its thusness.
Order and govern it, surely and aptly,
forgetting the Three-in-One, merging within without division.
Images emerge from pre-heaven,
the Dao is thus illuminated.

**Eulogy:**
The Great Void vast and distant,
all that is moved returns to it.
Heaven’s truth has its time,
impartial and without favor.
Clear and round like the jade balance,
resonant and roaming like the turning pearl.
Modeled on forms and appearances,
its images suit their objects.
Empty yet not full,
restrained yet not diminished.
Serene and cool,
mysterious and wondrous.
Supreme Clarity’s radiant splendor,
the Central Heaven’s Purple Tenuity.
Spirit enfolds utmost essence,
stellar visage gleams resplendent.

*End of the Third Scroll of the Supreme Clarity’s Great Mystery Collection*
*Beginning of the Fourth Scroll of the Supreme Clarity’s Great Mystery Collection*

**Lord Guanshe Shanyuan’s Inscription on the Golden Radiance and Jade Countenance of the Grand Beginning**

The noble person establishes conduct and practices the Dao, revering state laws and devoutly upholding the Mysterious Truth. They eradicate cravings and desires, casting aside the clamor of worldly dust. Through accumulated merit, they succor orphans and care for widows; through layered deeds, they cherish the aged and pity the poor. They look up to the virtuous without slackening, and lift the stubborn and indolent without arrogance. Harmony above and concord below—establishing virtue with compassion as its root. Inner rectitude and outward integrity—the Supreme Dao takes purity and stillness as its gate. When affairs are many, the heart finds no inner ease; when thoughts are severed, the mind does not wander outward. To halt excess and guard against loss, one must discern the moment for advance and retreat. Dwelling in peace, one contemplates peril, thereby distinguishing the principles of survival and ruin. Being and non-being mutually aid each other; movement and stillness share a single source. Stillness is called the Dao; movement is called the spirit. Silent yet responsive, moved yet without intent. Penetrating the primordial to replenish qi, fathoming the profound and luminous. Gathering the radiant yang soul in pure brilliance, transforming the yin po to reveal celestial truth. Stars congeal in mysterious illumination, the Dao releases its blossoming fragrance. Delving into the ultimate principle, one may die at dusk after hearing it at dawn. Thus, there is death yet no perishing—why envy Qi’s three sublime attainments? Not that there is no long life and enduring vision, but one does not scheme for Lin Lei’s century of years. Why not reflect: having form entails suffering, and one ultimately falls into the abyss of emptiness; only without appearance and form does one transcend beyond images. Diligently guard and cultivate merit—once merit is achieved and fame attained, shedding the mortal frame to ascend as an immortal is scarcely difficult.

**Eulogy:**
The Supreme Ultimate soars vast and distant,
its abyssal depths profoundly mysterious.
One qi waxes and wanes,
and the myriad things are born.
A numinous breeze, elegant and fair,
a luminous moon, resplendent and bright.
Mountains conceal jade treasures,
grasses split to reveal golden ornaments.
Nourishing an entire realm,
moistening and fostering a hundred streams.
Without intent, all is wondrous;
with desire, one approaches the brink.
Deluded, one becomes a ghost;
awakened, one ascends as an immortal.
Emerging from the boundless,
its image precedes heaven.

**Inscription on the Pure Heart of the Grand Abyss’ Celestial Boundary**

The Dao is silent yet unceasing,
responding and transforming without fixed form.
Virtue is manifest yet not forceful,
adapting to change with proper place.
Establishing images reveals the principles of sun, moon, heaven, and earth;
stabilizing hexagrams embodies the mechanisms of yin-yang, closure, and openness.
The fullness within *Kan*:
in heaven, it is the moon;
in humans, it is the ear.
The ear can perceive the sounds of thunder, wind, and rain—
this is called hearing and knowing, the mark of sageliness.
The emptiness within *Li*:
in heaven, it is the sun;
in humans, it is the eye.
The eye can discern the beauty of mountains, marshes, and waters—
this is called seeing and knowing, the mark of spirit.
Looking up, one models oneself on heaven;
looking down, one models oneself on earth.
In profound stillness, one observes images in transformation;
through transformation, one fathoms the causes of darkness and light.
Tracing beginnings and returning to endings,
one thus understands the discourse on life and death.
The *Book of Changes* says: "Probe the obscure and seek the hidden,
hook forth the deep and reach the distant."
The distant cannot be exhausted,
the near cannot be measured.
Vast and dim, none can know
why it is so, yet so it is.
To diminish or expend it
does not lose its essence.
To trust and uphold it
does not reveal its form.
Heaven endures, earth persists—
who can claim merit for high ascent?
Those who uphold the Dao
yet lack steadfast resolve,
turning back midway—
this is what it means.

**Eulogy:**
Embracing the divine splendor of the horizontal,
emerald shadows on jade peaks.

The toad’s radiance emerges in restraint, the sun’s glow sinks in the west.
The Dao illumines the mysterious realm, virtue aligns with the celestial pivot.
Clouds bathe in snowy purity, primordial qi purifies the heart.
Drought-spirits descend, all sages arrive in unison.
Girded with gold, adorned with jade, treasured auspices fill their hairpins.
Light trails like white feathers, tones arise from cold jasper.
Gently striking the jade chime, the clear sound is raised again.

**Inscription of the Jade Dawn of Supreme Clarity:**
The Terrace of Supreme Clarity—nothing is born without transformation.
The Illuminated Sovereign of Images—no darkness remains unlit.
